URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS514830420	2017-06-29 08:38:14	8725	species	Long-eared Owl	Asio otus			X				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Nye	US-NV-023		9			Smoky Valley	L6031937	P	38.6552536	-117.1507144	1933-06-06		obsr939641	S37864790	Incidental	P20	EBIRD				1	0		0	1	0			Observed by Jean M. Linsdale: "Clues as to the probable function of the dome on the nest were obtained by me, June 6, 1933, in Smoky Valley, Nye County, Nevada. At dusk when the long-eared owls became active magpies near the camp showed much concern. Alarm notes were heard from three different magpie nest locations and birds were seen in flight. When- ever an owl flew up it was followed closely by a magpie. In this locality an owls nest was situated usually close to each magpie nest. The owls did practically all of their foraging at night when the magpies probably slept, and, hence, they most likely required some special protection. This was about the time for the young of both species to leave the nest."

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS104502928	2018-08-04 09:04:36	8725	species	Long-eared Owl	Asio otus			1				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Washoe	US-NV-031		15			NV: Mogul: Truckee River	L234517	P	39.5069669	-119.9319417	2011-01-01	11:45:00	obsr18218	S7349646	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	75	4.828		3	1		0	1	0			First time I've seen a Long-eared Owl in this area.  South side of Truckee River, by the upper ditch.  We actually flushed it by mistake from a roost by the ditch.  It flew ahead of us, perched briefly, repeated, repeated again, got the attention of some Black-billed Magpies, and flew uphill, eventually perching on a rock a couple hundred meters away.  I got a few photos, but the bird is very small in them.  Quick appearance - similar to Great Horned Owl.  Observed long ears.  Fairly large, but compared to magpies did not seem as large as Great Horned Owl.  In flight, white on lower surface of wing, with very distinct dark patch on leading edge of wing at base of primaries, and dark wing tip.  Dark patch on upper surface of wing also visible in one of my photos.  Wings appeared very long and relatively slender compared to Great Horned Owl.

The noise then proceeded into my neighbor's yard.  I went in to my backyard and peered up into my neighbors Hawthorne tree where the commotion seemed to be centered and a group of birds just flushed from.   I could barely see a barred tail and I thought it must be an Accipiter getting everyone aggitated. I would never have thought I would see a Long-eared Owl as a yard bird.
